
5e Duets/
SALTMERE PORT OPERATION - SESSION SUMMARY Mission Context: 
Following the Thornhaven rescue, Johannes and Kessa tracked the slaving 
operation to Saltmere Port. Intelligence gathered: Harbor Master Voss 
coordinates local operations, Captain Drevik commands the slave ship Iron 
Tide (arrives dawn tomorrow), Commander Gharash oversees regional 
operations for Verminaard. Approximately 40-50 prisoners held in cells 
beneath eastern warehouse. 20+ guards total, some conflicted about their 
work. Key Ally: Garrick - conflicted guard who provided intel. He and 3 others 
(Tomms, Rickard, Olev) will create distraction at dawn when ship arrives. 
Garrick covering for tonight's activities. Voss Assassination (Successful): * 
Midnight ambush at warehouse loading dock * Swam in using Cloak of Manta 
Ray + Gillweed extract (no traces) * Sleep grenade dropped both bodyguards 
* Hex + dual Eldritch Blast wounded Voss (26 damage) * Rope of 
Entanglement restrained him * All three eliminated, bodies weighted and sunk 
in harbor * Looted: 80 gold, warehouse keys, Voss's rapier (magical, now 
Kessa's), bronze Takhisis medallion, sealed letter Letter Intel: Ship arrives dawn. 
Voss's cut was 30 gold per prisoner. Gharash inspecting operations "within the 
week." Operation is expanding. Current Combat - Warehouse: Used Minor 
Illusion (Voss's voice) to lure 4 guards up from holding cells. Surprise round 
eliminated 2 guards (Kessa's sneak attack + Johannes's Hex/EB combo). 2 
guards remaining, just realized they're under attack. Initiative Order: * Kessa: 
19 * Johannes: 15 * Guards (2): 9 Current Status: * Johannes: 39/39 HP, 2/2 
spell slots (Hex active on dead guard, can transfer) * Kessa: 38/38 HP, new 
magical rapier * Location: Main warehouse floor, ambush position near 
stairway to cells * Time: Just past midnight, ~6 hours until ship arrives * Items: 
1 sleep grenade remaining, 2 antidotes, Rope of Entanglement (used, 
recovered) Round 1 - Kessa's turn Ready to continue!

Dec 5
WAREHOUSE AMBUSH - ROUND 1
KESSA'S TURN
The two remaining guards stumble back, shields raised, trying to process what 
just happened. Their companions lie dead at their feet, and the "Harbor 
Master's" voice that lured them up has vanished into threatening silence.
Kessa moves like smoke, her new rapier singing as she darts forward. The 
blade feels perfectly weighted, responsive in a way her old weapon never was.
Kessa's Attack Roll (Sneak Attack advantage - surprise situation):
*	First roll: 16 + 6 = 22 to hit
*	Second roll (advantage): 11 + 6 = 17
The rapier finds the gap between breastplate and gorget. The guard gasps, 
clutching at his throat as blood wells between his fingers.
Damage Roll:
*	Rapier: 6 + 3 = 9 piercing
*	Sneak Attack: 2d6 = 5 + 3 = 8
*	Total: 17 damage
The guard drops to one knee, still alive but badly wounded (5 HP remaining). 
His companion backs toward the warehouse doors, clearly weighing whether 
to raise an alarm.
 
JOHANNES'S TURN
Your move. The Hex curse still thrums in your consciousness, its dark energy 
seeking a new target after the guard's death. One guard is wounded and 
kneeling, the other is backing toward the exit-and potential reinforcements.
Your resources:
*	Hex ready to transfer (bonus action)
*	2/2 spell slots remaining
*	Perfect position for Eldritch Blast
*	Sleep grenade if needed (but risky with noise)
Tactical considerations:
*	Wounded guard might surrender
*	Healthy guard heading for doors (30 feet away)
*	Unknown number of guards still below in cells
*	Need to keep this quiet if possible
What's your action?
Hex and Double EB for healthy guard

JOHANNES'S TURN

Hex Transfer (Bonus Action): Curse moves to healthy guard fleeing

Your hands weave the familiar patterns, eldritch energy crackling between

*	Attack Roll: 14 + 7 = 21 to hit ?

The first bolt catches him between the shoulder blades. He staggers but keeps 
moving.
Second Eldritch Blast:
*	Attack Roll: 18 + 7 = 25 to hit ?
*	Damage: 8 + 4 (Agonizing Blast) = 12 force damage
The second bolt punches through his back and erupts from his chest in a spray 
of purple-white energy. He drops face-first, sliding the last few feet toward the 
doors before going still.
 
GUARDS' TURN
The wounded guard on one knee looks at his three dead companions, then at 
Kessa's blood-slicked rapier, then at your still-glowing hands.
Wisdom Save (DC 10 to avoid being frightened):
*	Roll: 6 - 1 = 5 (fails)
His shield clatters to the floor. His sword follows.
"Please," he gasps, one hand still pressed to his bleeding neck. "I got a family 
in Hillsford. Kids. I-I didn't sign up for this slaving business, just needed the 
coin..."
 
ROUND 1 COMPLETE
Current Status:
*	3 guards dead, 1 surrendered (wounded, 5 HP)
*	Warehouse main floor secured
*	Hex active on dead guard at doors (can transfer)
*	No alarm raised yet
*	Prisoner cells still below with unknown guard presence
The surrendered guard trembles, blood seeping through his fingers. He's 
genuinely terrified and seems truthful about his family.
What do you do with him?
Take him back into the cells and lock him up. Check the conditions of the rest 
of the captured.
Dec 5
SECURING THE WAREHOUSE
PRISONER PROCESSING
"You'll live if you cooperate," you tell the guard, producing a length of rope. 
"Try anything and you won't see those kids again."
Kessa keeps her rapier ready while you bind his hands efficiently-tight 
enough to hold, loose enough he won't lose fingers. He doesn't resist, just nods 
frantically.
"How many guards below?" you ask quietly.
"T-two," he stammers. "Marcus and Joff. They're probably wondering what 
happened to us..."
 
DESCENDING TO THE CELLS
The stairway leads down into torch-lit dimness. The air grows thick with the 
smell of unwashed bodies, fear-sweat, and waste buckets. Stone walls weep 
moisture.
You reach the bottom to find a guard station-empty, the two guards likely 
patrolling. The holding area sprawls before you: a dozen cells lining both walls 
of a long corridor. Faces press against bars.
Perception Check (Johannes): 11 + 1 = 12 Perception Check 
(Kessa): 16 + 4 = 20
Kessa touches your arm, gestures down the corridor. Two guards at the far 
end, backs turned, checking cells. They haven't heard you yet over the 
prisoners' murmuring.
 
THE PRISONERS
Your torchlight reveals the cargo Voss was preparing to ship:
Count: Approximately 45-50 people crammed into cells meant for half that 
number.
Condition:
*	Malnourished - visible ribs, hollow cheeks
*	Dehydrated - cracked lips, listless movements
*	Injured - untreated cuts, bruises from rough handling
*	Terrified - some cower at your approach, others watch with desperate 
hope
*	Sick - you hear coughing, see fever-bright eyes
Demographics:
*	Mostly civilians from Thornhaven and surrounding villages
*	Mix of ages-young adults to elderly (no young children, mercifully)
*	A few look like they might have been town guards or militia
*	Several wear the simple clothing of farmers, craftspeople, merchants
Cell Conditions:
*	Packed 4-6 per cell designed for 2
*	Single waste bucket per cell (overflowing in some)
*	No bedding, prisoners sleeping on stone
*	Water buckets nearly empty
*	Iron bars rusted but solid
 
One woman near the front grips the bars, recognizing hope when she sees it. 
"Please," she whispers hoarsely. "Are you... did someone send help?"
Meanwhile: The two guards at the far end are still oblivious, about 60 feet 
away. Your bound prisoner stands silent beside you, not daring to raise alarm.
What's your approach?
*	Deal with the two guards first (stealth or direct)
*	Start releasing prisoners (but guards will notice)
*	Send Kessa to handle guards while you prep prisoners
*	Other strategy?
Remember, Devils Sight, no lights.

DESCENDING TO THE CELLS

Kessa moves close, one hand on your shoulder to guide herself. "Can't see a

THE SCENE BELOW
Through the absolute darkness, you see everything clearly:
Guard Station: Empty desk with logbook, ring of keys hanging on wall, two 
chairs.
The Corridor: Stretches 80 feet, cells lining both sides. Torches in sconces 
provide light for the guards-making them night-blind and you invisible.
The Two Guards (60 feet away):
*	Standing in torchlight, completely unaware
*	One is writing something in a ledger
*	The other is eating an apple, leaning against the wall
*	Neither is armored-just leather jerkins and clubs
*	They're relaxed, bored, not expecting trouble
The Prisoners: 45-50 people as previously described. Most are sleeping 
fitfully. Those awake can't see you in the darkness beyond the torchlight's 
reach, but some sense movement.
 
TACTICAL ADVANTAGE
You have perfect surprise conditions:
*	You: See everything perfectly, invisible in darkness
*	Kessa: Blind but can follow your lead
*	Guards: Night-blind from torchlight, completely unaware
*	Bound prisoner: Terrified, compliant, blind
The woman who whispered earlier squints into the darkness, seeing nothing. 
She hasn't raised her voice-not wanting to alert the guards to whatever might 
be happening.
 
Your approach?
You could:

Hex (Bonus Action): Apple-eater cursed.
Your hands move in the familiar patterns, twin bolts of eldritch force

*	Attack Roll: 13 + 7 = 20 to hit ?

The second guard drops his quill, clutching his shoulder where the bolt burned

"What the-where-?!"
 
KESSA'S TURN (SURPRISE ROUND)
"Now, Keys!"

*	One zips past Apple-eater's head (he flinches)
*	Two spiral around Ledger-writer in opposite directions
*	One hovers right at eye level between them
The guards spin, trying to track multiple threats, clubs raised uselessly. They 
still can't see you-just mysterious lights appearing from nowhere and 
invisible attackers in the dark.
"It's a wizard!" Apple-eater shouts. "Sound the-"

He collapses against the cell bars, sliding down to sit heavily. Still conscious

He's wounded, terrified, and can't see his main attacker in the darkness. He

"Demon! There's a demon!" He drops his club and scrambles away from

JOHANNES'S TURN

*	Attack Roll: 11 + 7 = 18 to hit ?

Ledger-writer spins toward the source of the blasts-still seeing nothing-as

LEDGER-WRITER'S TURN
He's wounded (17 damage total), alone, his partner dead, facing an invisible

His club clatters to the floor. "I surrender! Don't-please-I'm done!" His

Dec 5
SECURING THE CELLS
SEARCHING THE GUARDS
You step forward from the darkness, and several prisoners gasp as you 
seemingly materialize from nothing. Kessa's Dancing Lights illuminate your 
work as you search both wounded guards.
Ledger-writer's possessions:
*	8 gold pieces
*	Simple iron key (cell key-matches the ring on the wall)
*	Half-eaten bread and cheese in his pocket
*	Wooden club (standard)
*	Waterskin (half full)
Bound guard from upstairs (re-search):
*	12 gold pieces
*	Small knife (already confiscated)
*	Letter from someone named "Mara"-his wife, talking about their 
children's upcoming harvest festival performance
 
CELL ASSIGNMENT
You guide both wounded guards to an empty cell in the middle of the 
corridor-one that gives them no angle on the exit or guard station. Ledger-
writer limps along without resistance. Your original prisoner still clutches his 
bleeding neck.
Kessa's Medicine Check (binding their wounds):
*	Roll: 14 + 1 = 15
She tears strips from their shirts and binds the worst wounds. "You'll live," she 
says flatly. "Assuming you stay quiet and cooperative."
Both men nod frantically. You lock the cell door with a satisfying clunk.
"What happens to us?" Ledger-writer asks quietly.
 
THE GUARD STATION
With the immediate threat neutralized, you examine the area more carefully:
Key Ring on wall: Contains keys for all twelve cells plus what looks like a 
master key.
Logbook on desk (open to today's entries):
Day 47 - 49 prisoners total
- 3 more from western villages arrived 
- Old man (cell 7) died overnight - disposed
- Iron Tide confirmed for dawn delivery
- Captain Drevik expects 50+ for transport
- Harbor Master says final payment on delivery
Additional notes in margins: Guard rotation schedules, meal times (twice 
daily-thin gruel), prisoner behavioral notes ("cell 4 troublemakers," "cell 9 
cooperative").
Supplies: Stack of wooden bowls, water buckets, the bare minimum to keep 
people alive for transport.
 
THE PRISONERS
The woman at the front cell speaks again: "I'm Mera. From Thornhaven-we 
were taken three days ago." She looks at the others. "Most of us are from there 
or the villages nearby. Some have been here over a week."
Faces press against every cell bar now, hope and fear warring in their 
expressions. They're weak, frightened, but you can see the spark of survival 
still burning.
Tactical situation:
*	2 guards secured, 4 dead upstairs
*	~6 hours until Iron Tide arrives at dawn
*	47 living prisoners needing evacuation
*	Unknown if other guards will check in during the night
*	Bodies upstairs need handling
*	Garrick and his allies creating distraction at dawn
What's your next move?
Free Mera and then Visit Cell 4 - the troublemakers first.
Dec 5
LIBERATING THE PRISONERS
FREEING MERA
You take the key ring from the wall and approach her cell. The lock clicks 
open-the first taste of freedom in three days.
Mera stumbles out, legs unsteady from confinement. She's in her thirties, 
wearing the practical clothes of a Thornhaven shopkeeper, now filthy and 
torn. Despite her condition, there's steel in her eyes.
"Thank you," she says simply, then steadies herself against the bars. "What do 
you need from me?"
Kessa offers her the waterskin. Mera drinks deeply, then wipes her mouth. "I 
can help organize people once you let them out. Some are in bad shape-the 
elderly, the sick. We'll need to move carefully."
 
CELL 4 - THE TROUBLEMAKERS
You approach the fourth cell on the left. Five prisoners inside, all young men 
in their twenties. Unlike the others who look beaten down, these five have a 
different energy-coiled, angry, waiting.
One steps forward as you approach. Broad-shouldered, farmer's build, 
bandaged knuckles. He's been fighting.
"About damn time someone showed up," he says, voice low but intense. "I'm 
Garrett. These are my brothers-Finn, Cole-and our friends Jax and Petyr." 
He gestures to the others. "We're from Hillsford village. Took eight of 
Verminaard's bastards to bring us down."
The others nod. They're injured but not broken-bruised faces, split lips, but 
their eyes are sharp and calculating.
Garrett continues: "We've been planning. Once that ship arrives, we 
figured we'd try something during the transfer-create chaos, maybe some of 
us could escape." He looks at you directly. "But you've got something better 
planned, yeah? We can fight. We want to fight."
Finn (younger, leaner) adds: "We know this dock. Grew up fishing here 
before Verminaard's forces moved in. We know the warehouse layouts, the 
alleys, where guards patrol."
Cole (the quietest one) speaks up: "And we've got scores to settle. They 
killed our da when we resisted."
The five of them watch you with desperate intensity-men who've been caged 
like animals and are ready to bite back.
 
Mera observes quietly: "They've been talking about fighting since they 
arrived. The guards beat them twice for 'insubordination.' Some of the other 
prisoners think they're reckless... but they've got spirit."
 
What do you tell them?
Current tactical situation:
*	Dawn is ~6 hours away
*	Garrick's distraction will happen when ship arrives
*	47 prisoners to evacuate
*	These five want to fight, not just run
*	They have local knowledge of Saltmere Port
Do you:
*	Recruit them for the fight?
*	Tell them to focus on protecting other prisoners during evacuation?
*	Get their intelligence about the dock layout?
*	Something else?
Real violence is foiling Verminaard's plans, not killing down-on-their luck 
humans. Besides, I am sure your da would want you to care for the women 
and children first, not spit yourselves on the first swords someone swings at 
you. Get these folks out and then we can talk.
Dec 5
CELL 4 - REALITY CHECK
GARRETT'S REACTION
Your words land like cold water. Garrett's jaw tightens, and for a moment you 
think he might argue-but then something shifts in his expression. The hot 
anger cools into something harder, more useful.
"You're right," he says quietly, glancing at his brothers. "Da always said anger 
without purpose just gets you killed." He looks back at you. "We get people 
out. That's the mission."
Finn nods slowly: "Foiling their whole operation-that's the real revenge. 
Not just... swinging at whoever's in front of us."
Cole's voice is thick: "Da would clip us all upside the head for putting 
vengeance before helping folk who need it."
Jax (the stockiest one) cracks his knuckles: "Still wouldn't mind 
putting down anyone who gets in the way of the evacuation though."
Petyr (youngest, maybe 20) adds: "And we do know the docks. The safe 
routes out, where to avoid patrols. That's useful, yeah?"
 
GARRETT'S OFFER
Garrett extends his hand through the bars. "You've got our help. Proper help-
getting people out safe, using our heads instead of just our fists."
He pauses, then continues: "But answer me this-what happens after? Once 
we're out, Verminaard's forces are still here. Saltmere's still under his thumb. 
Do we just... run and hope they don't come hunting for us?"
The question hangs in the torchlit air. It's practical, not confrontational-he 
wants to understand the bigger picture.
Mera speaks up from behind you: "He's asking what I think we're all 
wondering. You came for us, which means you're fighting Verminaard 
somehow. What's the actual plan? Just rescue and scatter? Or is there more to 
this?"
The other prisoners are listening now-those close enough to hear are 
watching your exchange with Garrett with intense interest.
 
How do you answer?
The truth is complex:
*	You need tribute for your patron (though they don't need to know that)
*	Verminaard's operation is expanding
*	Gharash is coming "within the week"
*	The regional slave network needs disrupting
*	These people need somewhere safe to go
What do you tell them about the bigger picture?
Verminaard is too big a force for anyone to take on by themselves. Get 
yourselves to Haven, we can begin to form some kind of resistance there. And 
you can swell the ranks by telling those who resist your story far better than 
we can. We have plans, though. Voss has already paid his dues, it sounds like 
this captain whatever his name is, has a past due death tax he wasn't aware he 
owed and we aim to collect.
Dec 5
SETTING EXPECTATIONS
THE RESPONSE
Your words carry the weight of hard truth. Garrett's eyes sharpen-he 
recognizes someone who's actually thought this through, not just swinging 
wildly at shadows.
"Haven," he repeats, nodding slowly. "Makes sense. It's far enough from 
Verminaard's main forces, close enough to reach. And if the stories are true, 
there are others gathering there who want to resist."
Finn grins darkly: "Voss paid his dues? Good. That bastard watched them 
drag our da away and just... counted his gold."
Mera's voice is quiet but carries: "Captain Drevik. That's the name you're 
looking for. He commands the Iron Tide-he's the one who actually ships us. 
Voss just collected the merchandise." Her face hardens. "Drevik's got blood on 
his hands from a dozen ports."
Garrett extends his hand again through the bars: "Then we're with 
you. We get everyone to Haven, we spread the word about what happened 
here-about people actually fighting back. And you..." He meets your eyes. 
"You make sure that ship captain doesn't sail away clean."
Cole speaks up: "There's probably twenty families between Hillsford and 
Thornhaven who'll want to hear our story. Who'll want to know there's a place 
to gather, a chance to push back."
Jax adds: "And we can help organize the evacuation. Get people moving in 
the right direction, keep them together. We're no good scattered."
 
PETYR'S PRACTICAL QUESTION
The youngest of them steps forward: "How are we actually getting out? Dawn's 
maybe six hours away. That's 47 people-some sick, some old, some who can 
barely walk. Saltmere's crawling with Verminaard's troops. Even with a 
distraction..."
He's not doubting-he's planning. Asking the right tactical questions.
Mera nods: "He's right. The distraction from your contact helps, but moving 
this many people? We need a route, a destination, and a way to keep them 
together without being spotted."
 
THE TACTICAL REALITY
They're looking to you for leadership now. The situation:
Assets:
*	Garrick + 3 guards creating distraction at dawn
*	Local knowledge from Garrett's group
*	~6 hours until ship arrives
*	Keys to all cells
*	Warehouse access
Challenges:
*	47 prisoners, various conditions
*	Unknown patrol schedules in Saltmere
*	Need to avoid raising alarm before dawn
*	Bodies upstairs will eventually be discovered
*	Verminaard's forces throughout the port
The Question: What's your evacuation plan?
Do you:
*	Release everyone now and start moving them immediately?
*	Wait until closer to dawn when Garrick's distraction begins?
*	Send scouts (Garrett's group?) to map the safest route?

MARNA'S DECISION
Persuasion Check (Johannes): 15 + 3 = 18
Marna drums her fingers once more, then nods decisively.
"Deal. We sail to the eastern warehouse, load your people from inside, and get

that dock one second longer than necessary."
You count out the gold-Voss's blood money finding a better purpose. Marna 
weighs the purse, then tosses it to Finn. "Secure that. And get us ready to sail."
She turns back to you: "We'll be at your warehouse in thirty minutes. Have

together, anyone who needs help identified beforehand, and someone who can 
keep order during boarding. Fifty people trying to rush onto a ship in the dark 
is how accidents happen."
She pauses. "And whatever you're planning for Captain Drevik? Make sure it 
happens after we're gone. I don't need the Iron Tide spotting us pulling away 
from those docks."

TRUSTING THE CHAOS
KESSA'S RESPONSE

RETURN TO THE WAREHOUSE
You arrive back to find organized efficiency. Mera has worked miracles.
The Scene:
The prisoners are arranged in groups near the loading dock entrance:
*	Group 1: Mobile, healthy adults who can board quickly
*	Group 2: Elderly and those needing assistance

Mera has even found some relatively clean cloth to make rough bandages and

Rickard speaks quietly: "Garrick told me everything. I've been..." He

He unbuckles his Dragon Army insignia and drops it on the floor. "I'm with

Garrick clasps his shoulder: "Welcome to the right side, old friend."
 
THE ARRIVAL
Twenty minutes later, exactly as promised, you hear the creak of rigging and 
the gentle splash of oars. The Wayward Gull glides silently up to the 
warehouse loading dock, her crew working with practiced efficiency.
Marna stands at the rail, surveying the scene. She spots Garrett and his 
brothers, and something in her stern expression softens slightly.
"Tomas's boys," she says quietly. "He'd be proud."
Then, louder: "All right, people. Listen carefully. Board in the groups your 
organizers have arranged. No pushing, no rushing. Families stay together. If 
you need help, say so immediately. We have a long sail ahead and I want 
everyone accounted for before we cast off."
Her crew moves like clockwork-Finn and Sera helping people aboard, 
another crew member checking them off, two more arranging people below 
deck with blankets and water.
 
THE BOARDING
The process takes twenty minutes-fast, efficient, surprisingly 
orderly.
You watch as:
*	Mera helps elderly women aboard, whispering encouragement
*	Garrett and his brothers lift those too weak to climb themselves
*	Children cling to parents, eyes wide with fear and hope
*	The sick are carried carefully to makeshift beds below deck
Rickard pauses before boarding, looking back at you: "Whatever 
you're planning to do about Drevik... make it hurt. For all of us who stood by 
too long."
Garrick is the last of the prisoners to board. He grips your hand firmly. "We'll 
spread the word in Haven. Tell them what you did here. People need to know 
that Verminaard can be beaten."
 
DEPARTURE
Marna does a final count, nods to Finn, and gives the order. "Cast off. Set 
course for Haven, full sail once we clear the harbor."
The Wayward Gull slips away from the dock like a ghost, her dark sails barely 
visible against the night sky. Within minutes, she's merged with the other 
vessels in the harbor-just another ship moving in the darkness.
Current Status:
*	Fifty-one people evacuated safely

KESSA'S COUNSEL
A MOMENT OF REFLECTION
Kessa sets down the disguise kit and looks at you seriously. The playful edge 
that usually colors her voice is absent.
"Before we commit to this, let me say what I'm thinking."
She paces, organizing her thoughts.
 
THE TACTICAL PERSPECTIVE
"The disguise will work-probably. From distance, in dim light, with 
confidence? Yeah. But it's not foolproof. If Drevik gets suspicious, if he's heard 
Voss is missing, if he asks questions we haven't anticipated... it could go 
sideways fast."
"The ship infiltration is doable. I've done riskier. The Manta Cloak is 
perfect for it. But once I'm aboard with explosives, I'm committed. If things go 
wrong with your impersonation while I'm below deck rigging powder kegs, 
we're both in trouble."
She sits on a crate, weighing options.
 
THE STRATEGIC PERSPECTIVE
"Here's what we've actually accomplished tonight: Freed fifty people. 
Killed Voss and dismantled his operation. Got four of his guards to defect. 
Stole his money and intelligence. Verminaard's slave pipeline through 
Saltmere is broken."
"That's a massive victory, Johannes. Real damage to his operations."
She gestures toward the harbor. "The Iron Tide arriving to find 
everything gone? That's already humiliating for them. Drevik reports back 
that the entire shipment vanished, Harbor Master is dead, guards are 
missing... Verminaard loses face, loses revenue, loses momentum."
 
THE RISK ASSESSMENT
"But if we try to take out Drevik too?"
She counts on her fingers:
"Best case: We sink his ship, kill him, and escape clean. Maximum damage, 
maximum message. Verminaard learns his people aren't safe anywhere.
Likely case: We damage the ship, maybe kill Drevik, but things get messy. 
Fighting, chasing, possibly getting trapped. We're good, but we're two people 
against a ship's crew plus however many guards respond to explosions in the 
harbor.
Worst case: The disguise fails, I'm trapped on the ship, and we're fighting 
our way out against overwhelming numbers while dawn breaks and the whole 
port wakes up."
 
THE PERSONAL PERSPECTIVE
She meets your eyes. "I'll follow your lead. You know that. If you say 
we're doing this, I'm with you. I trust your instincts."
"But I also know..." She pauses, choosing words carefully. "Your patron is 
always there, isn't it? The pressure to accomplish more, take more 
risks, claim bigger victories. And sometimes that pressure can make us 
choose the spectacular over the smart."
"We came here to rescue prisoners. We did that-better than I 
dreamed possible. Do we need to prove something else? Or is it enough 
that fifty-one people are sailing to freedom right now because of what we did?"
 
THE QUESTION
She spreads her hands. "So here's what I'm really asking: Are we doing 
this because it's the right tactical move that furthers our goals? Or are we 
doing it because it feels like we should go bigger?"
"**If you believe Drevik needs to die tonight-**that killing him accomplishes 
something essential-then let's do it right. I'll help you become Voss, I'll plant 
those explosives, and we'll send that bastard to the bottom of the harbor."
"**But if there's any part of you that's doing this because you feel like 
you should-**because bigger is always better, because your patron demands 
spectacle-then maybe we should consider that we've already won tonight. We 
could take Voss's intelligence, his gold, his blackmail material, and disappear. 
Live to fight another day when the odds are better."
She stands, waiting.
"What does Johannes think? Not the Warlock, not the cursed 
soldier-you. What do you think is right?"
 
What's your answer?
She's right about Drevik. KIlling him is just simple vengeance, and I don't get 
to throw that in the boys' faces, then ignore that advice myself. But, there is 
something we can do. If we stage it right, one of us on lookout and one in the 
warehouse, when the Iron Tide is sighted on the horizon, we should have a 
good estimate of when they would be drawing near to the warehouse. We 
could time the explosives to go off right as the Iron Tide arrives. Not to harm 
anyone, but for the shock value of the place going up just as they are getting 
ready to dock. We have more than enough time to get out of town without 
making ourselves noticable, and the confusion of the explosion makes it all 
the easier to cover our tracks. In fact, we can also take Rickard's gear, and 
whatever else is left and set it up to look like Garrick and his friends were 
caught in the blast, making it that much easier to cover their escape.
Dec 5
THE BETTER PLAN
KESSA'S REACTION

REFINING THE APPROACH
"Here's what that accomplishes:
One: Drevik and his crew arrive expecting routine business. Instead they get a

Three: By the time anyone pieces together what actually happened, we're

Four: We destroy the warehouse, all of Voss's records of other officials

Five: We take the intelligence that we want-the supply route maps, the

the blast
*	Slip out of Saltmere while every guard rushes toward the fire"
 
KESSA'S FINAL THOUGHT
"This is smart, Johannes. We're not throwing ourselves at unnecessary

She grins. "And honestly? The look on Drevik's face when his

Dec 5
THE REVISED CALCULATION

*	Precise timing means controlled destruction
*	We know exactly when/where we need to be
*	Don't risk civilian casualties from uncontrolled fires
*	The story of the explosion reaching Haven helps recruitment
Cons:
*	Less time to loot Voss's estate (though we could still do it)
*	Smaller window for escape before dawn
*	We're making assumptions about Iron Tide's arrival time
 
KESSA'S INSIGHT
"Here's what I'm thinking: What if we don't have to choose?"
She lays it out: "Voss's estate is probably in the merchant district-nicer part 
of town, away from the docks. That's maybe... 15-20 minute walk? We could:
1. Rig the warehouse now with a long fuse (2-3 hour burn) 2. Go raid Voss's 
estate while the docks are still quiet 3. Get back to observation point before 
dawn 4. Watch the Iron Tide arrive 5. The warehouse explodes on schedule 
(we just timed it, not triggered it) 6. Walk away in the chaos
We get the loot and the psychological warfare."
She pauses. "But there's a risk: If anyone discovers the warehouse situation 
early-before we're back from the estate-our fuse is already burning and we 
can't adjust timing. We'd be committed."
 
THE ESTATE QUESTION
"Do we even know where Voss lived?" Kessa asks practically. "And what

already looted?"
She gestures to the 120 gold and gemstones. "We've already got his

*	Personal wealth (more gold, jewelry, art)
*	Better intelligence (personal correspondence, maps)
*	Blackmail material on more officials
*	Possibly magical items he kept private
*	Documents about his connections
Or it might just be a nice house with furniture and his clothes. We don't 
know."
 
KESSA'S HONEST ASSESSMENT
"Look, I'm not saying don't loot the estate. I'm saying we should 
think about:
One: Do we know where it is? (Can find out from the guard station 
schedules-they list addresses)
Two: What's the actual expected value vs. risk? Breaking into a dead Harbor 
Master's house in a city on alert...
Three: Does it serve our actual goals? We need funds for Haven, yes. But 
we've got 210 gold plus gemstones already. Is the additional loot worth the 
additional exposure?
Four: Time management. We've got maybe 2-3 hours until dawn. Rigging 
explosives properly takes time. Looting an estate takes time. We can probably 
do both, but it's tight."
 
THE QUESTION
She looks at you seriously. "What's driving this decision, Johannes? Is 
it:
*	Practical need? We genuinely need more resources for Haven and the 
estate likely has significant wealth?
*	Thoroughness? We're already here, might as well take everything we 
can?
*	The curse? Your patron expecting maximum acquisition from every 
opportunity?
*	Something else?"
"Because here's my gut: We've had an incredibly successful night. We've 
won. Sometimes the smart move is to take the win and not push our luck."
She spreads her hands. "But I'll follow your lead. If you think the 
estate is worth it, let's find out where it is and go get it. Just want to 
make sure we're choosing with clear heads."
 
What's your call?
*	Rig warehouse now, raid estate, timed explosion at dawn?
*	Rig warehouse for immediate explosion, raid estate in the chaos?
*	Skip the estate, focus on the timed explosion plan?
*	Something else entirely?
And honestly-what IS driving this decision?
Considering that rapier you're carrying, I can almost guarantee Voss has more. 
And if he's up to his eyeballs with Verminaard, you can bet he has been 
stashing away more than he spends...just in case things go south. Remember, 
he is a cold, cruel beast. Let's take him for everything we can.

PROFESSIONAL PREPARATION

EXIT STRATEGY
The Routes:
Kessa sketches in the dirt with a stick:
"Three ways out of Saltmere from here:
Route 1 - North Road (Primary):
*	Main highway toward Haven
*	Well-maintained, fast travel
*	Risk: Most likely to have Dragon Army patrols
*	Advantage: Blend with merchant traffic
*	Our cover: Just travelers who left early
Route 2 - Coastal Path (Secondary):
*	Follows the shoreline west, then cuts north
*	Rougher terrain, slower
*	Risk: Isolated, harder to explain if stopped
*	Advantage: Less patrolled, more hiding spots
*	Our cover: Fishermen, coastal traders
Route 3 - Forest Trail (Emergency):
*	Cuts through woods southeast, loops back north
*	Longest route, roughest terrain
*	Risk: Could get lost, slower progress
*	Advantage: Almost no patrols, total concealment
*	Our cover: Hunters, foragers"
 
IF WE GET SEPARATED

Rally Point 2: If Rally Point 1 is compromised or you can't reach it-there's

Rally Point 3: If both fail-just get to Haven. I'll find you there, or you find

She meets your eyes. "But we're not getting separated. Understood?"

Phase 3 (3-10 minutes):
*	Once we're outside immediate dock area, assess pursuit
*	If clean: maintain normal travel pace
*	If pursuit: switch to Route 2 or 3
Phase 4 (First hour):
*	Put distance between us and Saltmere
*	Watch for Dragon Army roadblocks
*	Be ready to go off-road if needed"

Dec 5
THE CALM BEFORE THE STORM
THE MOMENT
You stand at the window of the abandoned warehouse, watching the harbor 
come alive with morning activity. Kessa beside you, both of you silent, 
breathing in sync.
The Iron Tide glides closer. 200 yards now. You can see Captain Drevik 
on deck-middle-aged, weathered, the look of a man who's made this run a 
hundred times. Routine. Expected. Profitable.
The warehouse waits. Innocent from outside. Inside, chemistry and 
physics doing their inexorable work. Fire consuming rope, inch by inch, 
closing the distance to powder and oil and destruction.
The docks bustle. A merchant arguing with a customs official. Dock workers 
hauling crates. A woman selling fish from a cart. A child running between 
buildings, laughing. Normal people, normal lives, about to witness something 
extraordinary.
You find yourself hoping-genuinely hoping-that they're far enough away. 
That the blast radius you calculated accounts for them. That your vengeance 
and justice don't create new victims.
Kessa seems to sense it. She doesn't say anything, just nods slightly. She's 
thinking the same thing.
 
THE DECOYS
Your mind traces back through the staging:
Six dead guards, arranged carefully:
*	Three at blast center (obliterated beyond recognition)
*	Two in the cells (crushed by debris)
*	One near the loading dock (failed escape attempt)
Personal effects scattered strategically:
*	Rickard's letter from his wife (heartbreaking authenticity)
*	Guard schedules showing they were on duty
*	Weapons, coins, dice, personal items
*	Dragon Army insignia on the bodies
The narrative writes itself: "Harbor Master Voss and his guard detail 
killed in catastrophic warehouse accident. Possible munitions mishandling. 
Investigation ongoing."
Garrick, Tomms, Olev, Rickard-their names on a casualty list. Their families 
(if any) will grieve briefly before learning the truth through resistance 
channels. They're already halfway to Haven, reborn as new people with new 
names.
Captain Marna spreads word she left early for northern fishing grounds. Just 
another sloop in a busy harbor.
The pieces fit. The story holds.
If it works.
 
THE IRON TIDE APPROACHES
150 yards. Crew preparing dock lines. Drevik giving orders.
A small delegation on the dock-Dragon Army officials, probably there to 
receive the "cargo." They're checking manifests, expecting Voss to greet them.
Voss, currently in the harbor with stones in his pockets.
100 yards. The ship begins its final approach, sails being furled.
Kessa whispers: "Ninety seconds. Maybe less."
Your hand rests on the windowsill. The wood is rough, real, grounding you in 
this moment. This choice. This action.
Fifty-one freed slaves.
A fortune that will fund resistance.
Intelligence that will save lives.
A message that will echo across Verminaard's territory: You are not 
untouchable. Your operations can be dismantled. Your people will turn 
against you.
Was it worth it?
You think of Johannes's curse. The demon expecting tribute. The annual price 
paid in blood and magic.
This time, the tribute is different. Not artifacts scavenged and surrendered. 
Not compliance with evil demands.
This time, you're taking. Breaking. Building something that fights back.
The curse still sits in your soul, dark and cold. But tonight-this morning-you 
bent it. Used it. Made it serve something beyond itself.
Maybe that's the answer. Not breaking the curse, but breaking 
yourself free within it.
 
THE EXPLOSION
BOOM.
The sound is incredible-a physical force that rattles the windows, echoes 
across the harbor, sends birds screaming into the sky.
The eastern warehouse erupts.
Fire and smoke billow upward in a massive column. The roof collapses inward. 
Support beams crack like thunder. Secondary explosions as the oil barrels 
ignite-WHOOMPH WHOOMPH WHOOMPH.
Black smoke from the tar barrels creates a pillar visible for miles.
The alchemist's fire adds unnatural green flames to the inferno.
The smoke bombs detonate-thick, choking, spreading across the dock.
It's spectacular.
 
THE CHAOS
On the Iron Tide:
Drevik and his crew stare in shock. The ship actually rocks from the 
shockwave. Crew members point, shout, scramble.
The ship's approach falters-they were heading straight for that dock, now 
engulfed in flames and smoke.
On the docks:
People scatter like ants. Screaming, running, some toward the fire to help, 
others away in panic.
The Dragon Army officials stand frozen for precious seconds, then start 
barking orders.
Guards run from all directions toward the disaster.
The civilians:
The fish seller grabs her cart, fleeing.
The merchant and customs official forget their argument, staring.
The child's mother scoops them up and runs.
From what you can see-no one was close enough to be hurt. The blast 
was contained, dramatic but controlled.
 
THE EXIT
Kessa touches your arm. "Now. While everyone's looking that way."
You move to the horses. Mount up smoothly, professionally. Two travelers 
spooked by the explosion, deciding to leave town before things get worse.
You join a small stream of civilians doing the same-heading north away from 
the chaos.
Behind you, Saltmere descends into pandemonium:
*	Fire bells ringing
*	Guards shouting
*	The warehouse burning like a beacon
*	Captain Drevik's ship circling, unable to dock
*	Dragon Army scrambling to understand what happened
No one looks at you.
No one stops you.
No one suspects.
You're just two more people fleeing trouble.
 
THE NORTH ROAD
A mile out. Two miles. Three.
The smoke column is still visible behind you, a black monument to the night's 
work.
Kessa finally laughs-quiet, relieved, triumphant.
"We did it. We actually did it."
She looks at you with genuine respect. "Fifty-one people free. A fortune 
secured. Voss dead. His operation destroyed. And we're riding 
away clean."
The morning sun breaks over the horizon, painting everything gold.
A new day.
What are you thinking, Johannes?
Next place we can quietly get off the road and out of sight, I want to see that 
chest open.

(which we won't, because they're too useful)
Intelligence value: Incalculable for resistance operations"
Kessa whistles. "We could equip a resistance cell. Fund operations for 
months. Bribe officials. Buy weapons and supplies. Set up safe 
houses."
She looks at you seriously. "Johannes, this changes things. This isn't 
just 'we did well.' This is 'we can actually make a difference' 
money."
 
THE RING
She hands you the Ring of Mind Shielding again.
"Put this on. Seriously." Her voice is firm. "Your patron can't read 
your thoughts or scry your location while you're wearing it. 
That's... that's freedom, Johannes. Real freedom, at least 
mentally."
She watches you carefully. "Unless you're worried it might anger them? 
Not being able to check in on you?"
 
THE ROAD AHEAD
The smoke from Saltmere is still faintly visible in the distance, but you're safe 
here, hidden, with more wealth than you've ever possessed.
Kessa asks the practical question: "Do we keep moving toward 
Haven today, or do we rest here for a bit? We've been up all night, 
pulled off an impossible heist, and we're carrying a fortune. Might 
be smart to:
*	Sleep in shifts
*	Inventory everything properly
*	Plan how to present this to the Haven resistance
*	Decide what we keep personal vs. what we contribute
*	Actually eat a proper meal
Or do we push on while adrenaline is high?"
She grins. "Either way, this is the best haul of my entire career. And 
I've had some good scores."
What's your call?
Let's push on and get to Haven as soon as we can. As for the ring? I doubt the 
Patron cares. As long as the Pact remains in place, his toying with me is just 
cruelty for cruelty's sake, and it will make it so much easier for me to be able 
to hand away the Disks when the time comes if I don't grow dependent on 
their influence.
Dec 5
THE PUSH TO HAVEN
KESSA'S NOD
She watches you consider the Ring of Mind Shielding, then set it aside 
deliberately.
"You're thinking long-term." There's respect in her voice. "The Disks 
give you relief now, but you can't keep them forever. Better not to 
get comfortable with freedom you can't maintain."
She packs the ring back carefully. "Smart. Disciplined. Though it makes 
me want to break your curse even more, you stubborn bastard."
 
MOUNTING UP
You pack everything securely, dividing the weight between the two Bags of 
Holding. The horses are rested, and you've got provisions from the inn.
The road stretches north toward Haven.
Kessa swings into her saddle with easy grace. "Let's put some serious 
distance between us and Saltmere. I want to be twenty miles out 
before they even finish sorting through the warehouse rubble."
She grins. "Besides, I'm dying to see Garrick's face when we show up 
in Haven with enough gold to actually fund a proper resistance."
 
THE JOURNEY BEGINS
You ride hard but smart-not so fast you draw attention, but maintaining 
steady ground-eating pace. The morning sun climbs higher, warming the day.
Behind you, Saltmere deals with its catastrophe:
*	Warehouse smoldering
*	Captain Drevik trying to explain to his superiors
*	Dragon Army investigators finding dead "guards"
*	The daughter discovering her father missing
*	Eventually, bodies in the harbor
None of it touches you now.
You're free. You're wealthy. You're ahead.

CORRECTION - THE RING
MY APOLOGIES!
You're absolutely right-I completely misread that. Let me correct:
You're saying WEAR the Ring of Mind Shielding specifically SO that you 
don't grow dependent on the Disks of Mishakal's protection. The Ring blocks 
mental intrusion/scrying, which helps you:
1.	Not rely on the Disks' divine shield as your only protection
2.	Maintain independence from both divine and demonic influence
3.	Make it easier to hand the Disks away when necessary, since you'll 
already have mental protection from another source
4.	Avoid getting comfortable with the temporary relief the Disks 
provide
The patron doesn't care because the pact itself is what binds you-blocking 
mental surveillance is just you protecting your thoughts, not breaking the 
contract.
 
CORRECTED SCENE
Kessa hands you the Ring of Mind Shielding.
You slip it on your finger. It's cool metal, surprisingly comfortable, and almost 
immediately you feel a subtle shift-like a door closing between your mind 
and the outside world. Not oppressive, just... private.
"Smart," Kessa says, understanding immediately. "The Disks protect you 
from the patron's influence, but you can't keep them forever. This 
way, you're building independence that doesn't rely on divine 
artifacts you'll have to give up."
She nods approvingly. "You're already preparing for the day you hand 
them over. Not getting comfortable with borrowed protection."
The Ring sits on your finger, unobtrusive but present. Your patron can still 
feel the pact-that binding is in your soul, not your mind. But 
your thoughts are yours now. Your plans, your doubts, your strategies-
shielded.
It's not freedom from the curse.
But it's a small, real piece of autonomy reclaimed.

SHADOW OF MOIL SYNERGY
The spell creates:
*	Flame-like shadows wreath your body (dim light in 10-foot radius, 
darkness beyond that for another 10 feet)
*	You're heavily obscured to others (they can't see you clearly)
*	Attackers have disadvantage on attacks against you
*	You have advantage on attack rolls
*	Any creature that hits you with melee takes 2d8 necrotic damage
With Devil's Sight, you see perfectly through your own darkness.
With One with Shadows, you can go invisible AFTER the spell ends 
if still in darkness.
With Maddening Hex, you're dealing AoE psychic while being 
nearly impossible to hit.

Two riders, unremarkable to any who might pass. Just travelers heading 
north, away from trouble.
But between them:
*	The liberation of fifty-one souls
*	The destruction of a slaving operation
*	A fortune that will fund a resistance
*	Intelligence that will save lives
*	And the unshakable partnership of shadow and steel
Kessa rides beside you, her new weapons gleaming in the sunlight, a slight 
smile playing at her lips.
You feel the Ring of Mind Shielding on your finger-a small piece of autonomy 
reclaimed.
The Disks of Mishakal rest against your chest-temporary divine grace.
And deep within, the curse still coils. Patient. Waiting.
But today? Today you won.
Haven awaits.
 
SESSION END
Phenomenal work, Clayn. This was an absolutely masterful 
session-tactical brilliance, moral complexity, incredible rewards, 
and perfect character development.
Until next time, when Johannes and Kessa reach Haven and the 
real resistance begins...

Dec 6
ARRIVAL IN HAVEN
THE APPROACH
Three days of hard riding bring you to Haven as the afternoon sun angles 
golden across the valley.
The city rises before you-larger than you expected, nestled in a natural 
defensive position among hills. Unlike the oppressed settlements you've 
passed through, Haven feels... alive. Hopeful, even.
Perception Check (Johannes): 15 + 1 = 16
You notice immediately:
*	Fortifications being reinforced (new timber, fresh earthworks)
*	Refugee camps outside the walls (organized, not desperate)
*	Patrol routes being walked by mixed groups (not Dragon Army 
uniforms)
*	Smoke from forges working overtime
*	People moving with purpose, not fear
Kessa whistles softly. "This isn't just a city holding out. This is a city 
preparing to fight back."
 
THE GATES
As you approach, guards intercept you-but not aggressively. A woman in 
practical leather armor, bearing a silver medallion of Mishakal, steps forward 
with two armed companions.
"Travelers," she says, assessing you both. "State your business in Haven."
Before you can answer, there's a shout from behind the guards.
"JOHANNES! KESSA!"
Garrett pushes through, his brothers Finn and Cole right behind him. They 
look different-cleaner, better fed, wearing simple but decent clothes instead 
of prisoner rags.
The guard's hand goes to her weapon. "You know these people, Garrett?"
"Know them?" Garrett laughs, almost manic with relief. "Captain Morna, these 
are the ones who freed us. Who destroyed Voss's operation. Who got us here."
 
CAPTAIN MORNA'S ASSESSMENT
The woman-Captain Morna of Haven's defense forces, you realize-studies 
you with new intensity.
"The Saltmere refugees have been telling... quite a story." Her voice is careful, 
measured. "Fifty-one prisoners freed. A warehouse destroyed. Dragon Army 
infrastructure crippled."
She pauses. "And substantial resources brought with them for the resistance, 
they claim."
Insight Check (Johannes): 12 + 1 = 13
She's skeptical but hopeful. She's seen too many people promise much and 
deliver little. She's also clearly in charge of vetting newcomers-protecting 
Haven from infiltrators.
"I'm going to need you to come with me," she says. Not a threat, but not a 
request either. "Commander Brightblade will want to meet you. And you'll 
want to meet her."
Kessa mutters quietly: "Brightblade? That name sounds familiar..."
 
GARRETT'S INTERJECTION
"They're legitimate, Captain," Garrett says earnestly. "I'd stake my life on it. 
They risked everything to get us out."
Morna nods. "Which is why they're getting an escort to the Commander, not a 
cell." She gestures to her companions. "Come. Your horses will be seen to. 
Your belongings will remain with you."
She notices your obvious magical gear, Kessa's weapons, the quality of your 
equipment. "You're clearly capable. Let's find out if you're also aligned with 
our cause."
 
THE CHOICE
You could:
1.	Go peacefully - This is standard vetting, and you have nothing to hide
2.	Demand to see the freed prisoners first - Verify they're actually 
safe
3.	Ask about "Commander Brightblade" - Who are you meeting?
4.	Be cautious but cooperative - Answer questions, assess the situation
5.	Something else
Kessa whispers: "We just rode into their city carrying a fortune and 
claiming to be resistance heroes. Of course they're careful. I would be too."
She shrugs. "But Garrett vouching for us helps. And honestly? I'm curious 
who's actually running this operation."
 
THE CITY AWAITS
Behind Captain Morna, Haven stretches out-a city preparing for war, filled 
with refugees, resistance fighters, and people who've chosen to stand against 
Verminaard.
Somewhere in there:
*	The freed prisoners you rescued
*	Garrick and his companions
*	The resistance leadership
*	And answers about what comes next
What do you do?
I go along with the captain, approving of the New security measures. There 
doesn't seem to be any reason to be concerned... yet.
Dec 6
INTO HAVEN
THE ESCORT
"Lead on, Captain," you say with a respectful nod. "Your caution is wise. We'd

Captain Morna's expression softens slightly-approval. "Sensible. Come."
Garrett grins and falls into step beside you. "You're going to like Commander

Inside:
*	Maps covering every wall (troop movements, supply lines, Dragon Army

*	Runners bringing reports, taking orders

And at the head of the table:
A woman in her late twenties, perhaps early thirties. She's wearing practical

COMMANDER LAURANA BRIGHTBLADE

Laurana Brightblade stands, studying you both with a warrior's assessment.

Dec 6
LAURANA BRIGHTBLADE'S STORY
THE COMMANDER'S TALE
Laurana gestures for you to sit at the table. Kessa takes position beside you, 
alert but respectful. The others in the room settle in-this is clearly something 
they've heard before, but it still commands attention.
"You asked who I am," Laurana begins, her voice steady. "My full name is 
Laurana Kanan, though I've taken my husband's name-Brightblade-as my 
own in honor of his sacrifice."
She touches the Solamnic medallion at her throat.
"I was born in Qualinesti, daughter of the Speaker of the Sun." She pauses, 
watching for your reaction to that. "Yes, elven royalty. Which meant nothing 
when the Dragon Armies came."
 
THE FALL OF QUALINESTI
Her voice remains controlled, but you hear the steel beneath:
"Verminaard's forces didn't conquer Qualinesti through military might alone. 
They used dragons. Ancient reds, greens, blues-creatures of nightmare 
backed by Dragon Highlords who wielded power I'd never imagined."
"My people fought. We lost. My father..." She stops, composes herself. "My 
father chose to stay behind, to buy time for refugees to escape. I never saw him 
again."
Garrett and the others are silent, respectful. They've heard this, but 
it clearly still moves them.
"I fled with survivors-thousands of us. Scattered across the continent. Many 
died on the roads. Others were captured, enslaved, shipped to places like..." 
She looks at Garrett. "...places like Saltmere's warehouses."
 
THE TRANSFORMATION
"I was a princess who'd never held a real weapon. Who'd studied music and 
diplomacy and the arts." A bitter smile. "Useless skills when your world 
burns."
She draws her longsword-the movement practiced, professional. "I learned to 
fight. I met others who'd lost everything. Refugees, soldiers, knights who'd 
seen their orders destroyed."
"One was Sturm Brightblade-a Solamnic Knight without a knighthood. 
His order was scattered, disgraced, hunted. But he lived by the Measure and 
the Oath as if the whole world still honored them."
Her voice softens. "He taught me that nobility isn't bloodline or title. 
It's choice. Choosing to stand when you could run. Choosing to protect when 
you could hide. Choosing to hope when despair is easier."
 
THE PRICE
"We married in secret, between battles. Three months later, he died holding a 
mountain pass so civilians could escape. Forty people lived because he stood 
alone against a Dragon Army patrol."
She sheathes the sword. "That was eight months ago."
The room is absolutely silent.
"I took his name. I took his cause. And I came to Haven because refugees were 
gathering here, leaderless and afraid. Someone needed to organize them. 
Turn fear into fury. Despair into determination."
She looks around the command center. "This isn't an army. Not yet. We're 
farmers and merchants and refugees who've learned to fight because we have 
no choice."
 
THE MISSION
Laurana leans forward, intensity in her eyes.
"Verminaard controls most of Ansalon now. His Dragon Highlords command 
armies, backed by chromatic dragons and dark clerics. They enslave 
populations, strip resources, crush resistance."
"Haven is a thorn. A gathering point. A symbol that not everyone has 
surrendered."
She spreads her hands over the maps. "We raid supply lines. Free prisoners. 
Protect refugees. Disrupt their operations however we can."
"We're not winning. But we're not losing either. And every day we survive, 
more people find their way here. More slaves get freed. More hope spreads."
 
THE ASSESSMENT
She looks at you directly now.
"Garrett says you freed fifty-one people from Saltmere. Destroyed a slaving 
operation. Killed a corrupt Harbor Master and turned four guards to our 
cause."
"Captain Morna's scouts report that Saltmere's eastern docks are gone-
burned to nothing. Dragon Army is scrambling. Commander Gharash is 
investigating personally."
A slight smile. "That's not refugee luck. That's capability."
"So now I've told you who I am-a princess who became a widow who became 
a soldier. Someone trying to build resistance from broken pieces."
She folds her hands. "Your turn. Who are you, Johannes Constantinius? What 
brings a warlock and his companion to Haven? And what do you really want?"
 
THE MOMENT
Everyone waits. Laurana has been honest, vulnerable even, sharing her losses 
and her mission.
Now she's asking for the same from you.
How much do you tell her?
*	The curse? Your demonic patron?
*	Your goals against Verminaard?
*	The Disks of Mishakal?

*	Everything? Some things? Strategic truth?

Dec 6
JOHANNES'S STORY - STRATEGIC 
TRUTH
YOUR RESPONSE
You meet Laurana's eyes directly-respect to respect, honesty to honesty.
"I'm Johannes Constantinius. A warlock, yes-bound by a pact I didn't fully 
understand when I made it, paying prices I'm still learning to calculate."
You keep your voice level, factual. "My companion is Kessa Darrow-rogue, 
bard, and the reason I'm still alive more times than I can count."
Kessa gives a slight nod of acknowledgment.
 
THE JOURNEY
"We came to this region following rumors of Dragon Army movements. At 
Firestorm Peak, we discovered an ancient gate-a portal to the Far Realm that 
cultists were trying to open. We stopped them, destroyed the gate, and 
prevented something... considerably worse than Verminaard from entering 
this world."
Laurana's eyes sharpen. "Firestorm Peak. We've heard reports-an entire 
cultist operation vanished overnight. That was you?"
"It was." You continue. "From there, we tracked Dragon Army activities to Xak 
Tsaroth-an ancient ruined city. We found more than soldiers there."
 
THE BLACK DRAGON
"An ancient black dragon named Khisanth ruled the ruins. She'd made 
arrangements with the Dragon Army-mutual non-interference, territory 
respected."
Captain Morna tenses. "You faced an ancient black dragon?"
"We negotiated," you say simply. "She was evil, yes, but lawful evil. Logical. 
She respected strength, intelligence, and-most importantly-keeping your 
word."
You pause. "We had something she wanted information about. She had 
knowledge we needed about Dragon Army operations in the region. We made 
a trade. Both sides honored it."
Laurana leans back slightly, reassessing. "You negotiated with an 
ancient dragon and walked away alive. That's... rare."
 
THE PATTERN
"After Xak Tsaroth, we tracked slave operations. We hit Thornhaven first-

Garrett interjects: "That's where they learned about Saltmere. From prisoners 
we freed."
You nod. "Saltmere was larger, more organized. Harbor Master Voss ran fifty

You choose words carefully. "We eliminated Voss and his operation.

THE RESOURCES
"We're not refugees seeking shelter," you say plainly. "We're fighters who've

point where working alone has limits."
You gesture to the maps around you. "You have organization, numbers,

Kessa adds quietly: "And about seventeen hundred gold worth of liquid 
assets, plus magical equipment and intelligence on Dragon Army supply 
routes and corrupt officials."
The room goes absolutely silent.
 
THE OFFER
"We came to Haven because you're building something real," you say. "Not 
just survival-actual resistance. Coordinated operations. Strategic thinking."
You lean forward. "I don't know if we can beat Verminaard. His forces are 
vast, his dragons are terrifying, his Highlords are powerful. But I know that 
scattered refugees hiding in the woods accomplish nothing."
"What we did at Saltmere? We could do that at a dozen other ports, supply 
depots, prison camps-if we had intelligence, coordination, and support."
You meet Laurana's eyes. "So here's my offer: Our capability, our resources, 
our experience-in service of Haven's resistance. We hit targets you identify. 
We fund operations you plan. We fight alongside people who've chosen to 
stand."
A pause. "In return, we want the same thing you do-to hurt Verminaard's 
operations, free his prisoners, and prove that resistance is possible."
 
THE UNSPOKEN
You haven't mentioned:
*	Your specific demonic patron
*	The yearly tribute curse
*	The Disks of Mishakal
*	Your longer-term goal of breaking the pact
But what you've said is true-strategically chosen truth that establishes 
capability, intent, and alignment without revealing vulnerabilities.
 
LAURANA'S REACTION
She's silent for a long moment, studying you. Then she looks at Captain 
Morna, who gives a slight nod.
"Seventeen hundred gold," Laurana says quietly. "That funds operations for

She stands, extending her hand across the table. "Johannes Constantinius. 
Kessa Darrow. Welcome to Haven's resistance."
Her grip is firm, a warrior's handshake.
"But understand-we operate with structure here. Chain of command. 
Coordinated strikes. No lone wolf heroics that compromise other operations." 
Her eyes are steel. "Can you work within that framework?"
 
How do you respond?
And somewhere in your Bag of Holding, the Disks of Mishakal rest-waiting 
for you to decide if this woman, this widow-turned-commander, might be

THE WAR ROOM

Option 3 - Strategic Strike:

4.	Defer to Laurana's experience with the region?
5.	Something else?
Kessa is watching the maps with interest, her tactical mind clearly 
working.
My immediate though: Gharash is in the open. Taking him down could 
significantly mess up Verminaards plans in this area. And we have access to 
info that could increase our odds of success.
Dec 6
THE GHARASH GAMBIT
YOUR PROPOSAL
"Gharash," you say, tapping Saltmere on the map. "He's exposed right now, 
investigating the warehouse destruction. Angry, probably operating with a 
smaller security detail than usual because he's moving fast."
You look up at Laurana. "And we have intelligence he doesn't know we have-
Voss's records, his communications, possibly routes and schedules."
The room goes very quiet.
 
IMMEDIATE REACTIONS
Captain Morna's eyes widen: "You're suggesting we assassinate a Dragon 
Army Commander? While he's actively investigating an attack?"
The dwarf officer-you learn his name is Thoric Ironforge-strokes 
his beard thoughtfully: "Bold. Insanely risky. But... strategic. Gharash 
coordinates the entire regional slave network. Without him, their operations 
fragment."
Laurana's expression is unreadable. She's thinking, calculating.
Kessa leans forward, energized: "Johannes is right. Gharash is off-
balance, focused on Saltmere. He's hunting for ghosts-dead guards he thinks 
died in an accident, a Harbor Master who 'disappeared.' He doesn't know 
we're the threat. He doesn't know we have his communications."
 
LAURANA'S ASSESSMENT
"If we succeed," Laurana says slowly, "we decapitate Dragon Army operations 
in this region. Supply lines collapse. Prison transports stop. Verminaard has to 
divert a new commander, reorganize everything."
She meets your eyes. "If we fail, or if we're traced back to Haven, Verminaard 
sends dragons and a full military response. This city-everyone in it-dies."
She's not dismissing the idea. She's weighing it.
"Tell me more. What intelligence do we actually have on Gharash? Movement 
patterns? Security details? Vulnerabilities?"
 
INTELLIGENCE REVIEW
Captain Morna pulls out Voss's documents you provided:
"From the warehouse records and letters, we know:
Gharash's Pattern:
*	Inspects operations personally (hands-on commander)
*	Travels with elite guard unit (10-15 soldiers, well-trained)
*	Uses a wyvern for fast transport (not a true dragon, but dangerous)
*	Paranoid about assassination-varies routes, unexpected arrivals
*	Based out of a Dragon Army command post near Thoradin"
From Voss's correspondence: "Gharash was expected 'within the week' of 
the Saltmere operation. That was five days ago. He's there NOW or arriving 
soon."
The elven scout adds: "Our contacts in Saltmere report Dragon Army 
activity spiked three days ago. Commander-level officer arrived by wyvern, has 
been interrogating survivors, inspecting the ruins."
 
THE TACTICAL REALITY
Thoric Ironforge lays it out:
"Gharash in Saltmere means:
Pros:
*	Known location (approximately)
*	He's focused on investigation, not defense
*	Smaller force than if he were at his command post
*	We have local intelligence from your recent operation
Cons:
*	Still has elite guards
*	Has a wyvern (mobile, dangerous)
*	Saltmere is Dragon Army territory now-reinforcements available
*	He's actively hunting for information about attackers"
He looks at you. "You just struck Saltmere five days ago. Going back into that 
hornet's nest to kill their commander? That's either brilliant or suicidal."
 
LAURANA'S HARD QUESTIONS
She's all business now, testing your plan:
"One: How do we confirm his exact location and movements?
Two: How do we get a strike team into Saltmere without being detected?
Three: How do we kill a paranoid commander with elite guards and a 
wyvern?
Four: How do we extract afterward without leading pursuit back to Haven?
Five: What's our contingency if this goes wrong?"
She crosses her arms. "I won't send people on a suicide mission for glory. If we 
do this, it has to be surgical. In, kill, out, no trail."
She looks at you and Kessa specifically. "You two just pulled off an 
impossible operation there. Could you do it again? Target a commander 
instead of a warehouse?"
 
KESSA'S TACTICAL INPUT
"It's doable," Kessa says, surprising you slightly with her confidence. "But not 
with a large force. Gharash will have sentries, counter-intelligence, detection. 
A big group gets spotted."
She traces routes on the map. "Small team. Maybe 4-6 people total. We use the 
intelligence to predict his movements, set an ambush away from his main 
force, hit fast, and disappear."
She looks at you. "Johannes and I could scout, gather current intel, identify 
the opportunity. But we'd need support-maybe a distraction, definitely 
extraction planning."
 
THE DECISION POINT
Laurana takes a deep breath.
"This is the kind of decision that defines a resistance. Play it safe-we survive 
but accomplish little. Take the shot-we either strike a massive blow or bring 
destruction down on Haven."
She looks around the room. "I want honest counsel. Should we attempt this?"
Captain Morna: "High risk, high reward. We need intelligence first."
Thoric Ironforge: "Dwarves don't shy from bold strikes. I say we plan it 
properly, then do it."
The elven scout: "We could use our Saltmere contacts to gather current 
intelligence on Gharash's location."
Garrett speaks up from the side: "These two freed fifty-one of us and 
burned down Voss's operation. If anyone can pull this off, it's them."
All eyes turn to you.
 
THE COMMITMENT
Laurana asks directly:
"Johannes. Kessa. If I greenlight this operation-if I commit Haven's 
resources to supporting this strike-are you willing to lead it? To go back into 
Saltmere, hunt a Dragon Army Commander, and kill him?"
"This isn't solo adventuring anymore. This is war. People's lives depend on 
your success or failure."
She extends her hand. "Are you in?"
 
What's your answer?
And do you want to:
1.	Commit immediately
2.	Request more intelligence gathering first
3.	Propose specific team composition
4.	Suggest alternative approaches
5.	Something else
This is a major decision point in the campaign.
Purpose the team: Garrick and his former guards, is willing. They know the

the better, before Gharash has time to solidify things and restore order.
Dec 6
OPERATION GHARASH - TEAM 
ASSEMBLY

Combat Capability:

THE NIGHT BEFORE
KESSA'S THOUGHTS
After the briefing concludes and the team disperses to prepare, Kessa catches 
your arm as you're heading to assigned quarters.
"Walk with me a minute?"
 
A QUIET CONVERSATION
She leads you to Haven's walls-a quiet section overlooking the valley as the 
sun sets. The view is beautiful, peaceful. Hard to believe there's a war 
happening.
She's quiet for a long moment, then:
"Johannes... we're about to assassinate a Dragon Army Commander. In a city 
we just burned part of five days ago. With a team of 'dead' men and a wyvern-
riding paranoid veteran as our target."
She turns to look at you. "I'm not having second thoughts. I'm in. But I want 
to make sure you are too."
Her expression is serious-genuinely checking in.
"This isn't like Voss. That was tactical, clean, we controlled every variable. This 
is walking into active Dragon Army territory to kill someone who's actively 
hunting for threats. The risk level is..."
She trails off, then laughs quietly. "Listen to me. I sound like I'm trying to talk 
you out of it. I'm not. I just want to make sure we're thinking clearly."
 
HER REAL CONCERN
"Here's what's actually on my mind," she says, leaning against the wall.
"Garrett and his people are good folk. They deserve a chance to matter, to 
make amends for standing by too long. But they're not soldiers. If this goes 
sideways-if Gharash's guards swarm us, if the wyvern gets involved, if 
reinforcements arrive-they're liabilities."
"You made the right call keeping them as support. But we need to 
be absolutely clear with each other: if things go wrong, we save ourselves 
first. We don't die trying to protect people who signed up knowing the risks."
She meets your eyes. "Can you do that? Because I've seen the way you look at 
them. Like they're people you're responsible for. And that's... good. It's right. 
But it can also get you killed."
 
THE TACTICAL REALITY
"Here's my professional assessment," she continues, slipping into mission-
planning mode:
"Best case: We use their intelligence, identify a perfect opportunity, strike 
when Gharash is isolated, and ghost before anyone realizes what happened. 
Clean, professional, textbook assassination.
Likely case: We identify an opportunity, it's not perfect but it's workable, we 
engage with some complications, and we have to fight our way clear. Messy 
but successful.
Worst case: Gharash is more paranoid than we expect, we can't isolate him, 
and we either abort or push anyway and face overwhelming odds."
She pauses. "I'm prepared for all three. Are you?"
 
HER DEEPER QUESTION
"And here's the thing I keep coming back to..."
She's choosing words carefully. "You've got a fiendish patron. You carry some 
kind of... I don't know, divine protection that I've never asked about because 
you haven't offered to tell me. You've got layers I don't fully understand."

2. Internal Tensions:

*	Ember (the dragon) also leaves periodically

THE CHALLENGE
One evening, Kessa spreads maps across your table:
"Here's the reality: Pax Tharkas isn't Saltmere. It's not even close."
She taps the fortress drawing. "Saltmere was a corrupt port with lazy guards 
and one paranoid commander. We killed six people and freed fifty prisoners."
"Pax Tharkas has 800 soldiers, a Dragon Highlord, and a red dragon. 
We'd need to free 600+ prisoners and get them through mountain 
passes while being pursued by dragons and armies."
She looks at you seriously. "This isn't an assassination. This is a military 
operation. It requires an army, coordination, planning, logistics, and a lot of 
luck."
She pauses. "Which means we can't do it alone. We need Haven's full 
support, probably allies from other resistance cells, and a plan that accounts 
for everything going wrong at least twice."
 
YOUR ASSESSMENT
After months of research, you understand:
Pax Tharkas is possible-but not yet.

GOLDMOON'S BLESSING
The cleric of Mishakal steps forward. She's carrying a staff topped with the

When she reaches you, she pauses. Her eyes study you-not suspicious,

"You carry a heavy burden, Johannes Constantinius. I sense darkness bound
